With increasing urban density and limited availability of land, Singapore has to strategize to prepare and adapt early to climate change.\nby Chi-Hwa Wang\nSingapore contributes to 0.11% of global emissions, and is taking initiatives to reduce carbon\u2028emissions, building on past mitigation efforts. The most significant contributor to the greenhouse gases (GHG) in Singapore is Carbon Dioxide (95.5%), followed by PFCs and N2O. In addition, the combustion of natural gas to generate electricity has been identified to be the main contributor (33.4%) to national GHG emission amongst other contributors including emissions from transportation and industrial activities. Under the Paris Climate change agreement, Singapore pledged to reduce Emissions Intensity (EI) by 36 % from 2005 levels by 2030 and stabilize emissions with the aim of peaking around 2030.\nTo achieve these ambitious targets, many efforts have been made to promote energy efficiency and environmentally friendly Singapore. Register now\nCurrent State of Waste Management in Singapore\nBeing a small, low lying island city-state, Singapore is naturally vulnerable to the impact of climate change. With increasing urban density and limited availability of land, Singapore has to strategize to prepare and adapt early to climate change.\nby Chi-Hwa Wang\nSingapore contributes to 0.11% of global emissions, and is taking initiatives to reduce carbon\u2028emissions, building on past mitigation efforts. The most significant contributor to the greenhouse gases (GHG) in Singapore is Carbon Dioxide (95.5%), followed by PFCs and N2O. In addition, the combustion of natural gas to generate electricity has been identified to be the main contributor (33.4%) to national GHG emission amongst other contributors including emissions from transportation and industrial activities. Under the Paris Climate change agreement, Singapore pledged to reduce Emissions Intensity (EI) by 36 % from 2005 levels by 2030 and stabilize emissions with the aim of peaking around 2030.\nTo achieve these ambitious targets, many efforts have been made to promote energy efficiency and environmentally friendly Singapore. Waste management is one of ...",

Climate Change and Energy Efficiency 4 Climate Change and Energy Efficiency \u2022 In October 2022, Singapore pledged to achieve net zero emissions by 2050, contingent on technological maturity and effective international cooperation. \u2022 We also announced that we will enhance our 2030 Nationally Determined Contribution (NDC) to reduce emissions to around 60 Mt CO2 eq in 2030 after peaking emissions earlier.\n\u2022 Since then, we have been focusing our efforts on implementation and delivering progress, to ensure that our climate targets remain backed by concrete policies and plans. \u2022 A key pillar of Singapore\u2019s strategy to mitigate GHG emissions is to improve energy efficiency across different sectors of the economy. \u2022 Singapore does not subsidise energy costs, and has taken steps to use a cleaner fuel mix for electricity generation, switching from fuel oil to natural gas. \u2022 At the start of 2024, we raised our carbon tax level to S$25 per tonne of emissions. We will progressively raise it to S$50-80 per tonne by 2030. 5 Climate Change and Energy Efficiency \u2022 Our current 2021 GHG emissions are around 54 MtCO2eq.\n\u2022 Industry is the largest energy consumer (both primary and secondary energy) at around 60% \u2022 Specifically for emissions from the chemical industry, particularly from industrial processes or non-fuel combustion sources (for example, flares and vents), we observed that the emissions are still growing, with CAGR of 6.7% from 2000-2016 and 21.3% from 2016-2022.\n\u2022 Note: An updated timeseries would be published for year 2000 to 2022 in Singapore\u2019s first Biennial Transparency Report (BTR1) after submission to the UNFCCC by end of 2024.\nSingapore\u2019s emission profile published on NCCS\u2019 website (2021 data) To give a sen...",

We will \nprogressively raise it to S$50 -80 per tonne  by 2030.\n5\nClimate Change and Energy Efficiency\n\u2022Our current 2021  GHG emissions are around 54 \nMtCO2eq.\n\u2022Industry is the largest energy consumer (both primary \nand secondary energy) at around 60% \n\u2022Specifically for emissions from the chemical industry, \nparticularly from industrial processes or non -fuel \ncombustion sources (for example, flares and vents), \nwe observed that the emissions are still growing, with \nCAGR of 6.7% from 2000 -2016 and 21.3% from 2016 -\n2022.\n\u2022Note: An updated timeseries would be published for year 2000 to \n2022 in Singapore\u2019s first Biennial Transparency Report (BTR1) \nafter submission to the UNFCCC by end of 2024.Singapore\u2019s emission profile published on NCCS\u2019 website (2021...",
